ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-item {
    counter-increment: list-counter-alpha;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-alpha, lower-alpha);
}

/* Level 3: Lowercase roman numerals */

    counter-reset: list-counter-roman;
}

    counter-increment: list-counter-roman;
}

ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list ol.enhanced-list .list-marker::before {
    content: counter(list-counter-roman, lower-roman);
}

element-container st-emotion-cache-kj6hex eu6p4el1" data-testid="stElementContainer" data-stale="false" width="auto"><div class="stMarkdown" data-testid="stMarkdown"><div data-testid="stMarkdownContainer" class="st-emotion-cache-1104ytp e1icttdg0"><p><strong>Processing file:</strong> Unit_6_Communication_and_Counselling.pdf</p></div></div></div><div class="stElementContainer element-container st-emotion-cache-kj6hex eu6p4el1" data-testid="stElementContainer" data-stale="false" width="auto"><div class="stMarkdown" data-testid="stMarkdown"><div data-testid="stMarkdownContainer" class="st-emotion-cache-1104ytp e1icttdg0"><p>UNIT SIX: COMMUNICATION AND COUNSELLING</p>
<p>This unit focuses on communication and counselling. In the last five units of this module you covered professionalism, fundamentals of nursing, adult nursing, paediatric nursing, critical care and operating room nursing. In this unit you are going to focus on communication and counselling.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unit-objectives">Unit Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unit-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this unit you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe the communication process</li>
<li>Describe the key contexts of communication</li>
<li>Describe barriers to effective communication</li>
<li>Describe essential organisational communication</li>
<li>Describe psychology</li>
<li>Describe counselling</li>
<li>Describe patient's rights and ethical issues</li>
<li>Describe approaches to counselling</li>
<li>Counsel target groups</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-1-defining-communication">SECTION 1: DEFINING COMMUNICATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-1-defining-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>You might have noted from the introduction that the first four objectives of this unit are on effective communication and the next four are on counselling. Therefore, this section will begin by focusing on communication, and later on counselling.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>State the definition of communication</li>
<li>Describe different types of communication</li>
<li>Explain the communication process</li>
<li>Describe the components of the communication process</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="communication">Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>To begin with, consider the following question: Think of the number of times you interact with patients each day. Can you count that number?</p>
<p>Perhaps it is impossible to count. Well, the conversation you hold with your patients and even colleagues while exchanging views is called communication. So, it could be said that communication is the exchange of information between two or more persons who are interacting with each other in such a way that the information is understood. It can, therefore, be concluded that communication is the transfer of meaningful information and the establishment of commonality with the audience.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="types-of-communication">Types of Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Communication can be formal, informal or unconscious.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="formal-communication">Formal Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#formal-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Formal communication is any official method of communicating with people (employees) in an organisation. The communication may be passed orally or in written form. The message flows from top to bottom, for example, from the top management to staff at the lower levels, following the hierarchy or chain of command in the particular organisation.</p>
<p>Formal communication mainly involves giving instructions to be followed and clarifying the roles of staff in the organisations. It also emphasises the use of available resources to achieve the desired goals. Formal communication flows in three directions, namely:</p>
<ul>
<li>Downward communication</li>
<li>Upward communication</li>
<li>Horizontal communication</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="downward-communication">Downward Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#downward-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>This is where the communication flow comes from top management to the lowest level. The communication channels used include oral messages, telephone calls, written communication in the form of circular letters, memoranda, pamphlets or posters. The main advantage of downward communication is that it</p>
<p>Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Bishops Computers</p>
<p>is received immediately and is not distorted. For example, the district public health nurse may request the nurse working in a health centre to submit a written report on a monthly basis to their office.</p>
<p>The main disadvantage of downward communication is that it is unidirectional, that is, there is no return path for communication, this delays feedback. For example, a nurse in charge of a unit may decide to keep a recommendation report for promotion in the file and delay sending it to the Public Service Commission for approval. Downward communication within the Ministry of Health is illustrated in the diagram (right).</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-87d1b40f.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="upward-communication">Upward Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#upward-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This type of communication flows from staff at lower and middle levels to the top management. This provides feedback regarding organisational progress, a consultative forum to improve the quality of service and a means for staff to request clarification of goals and/or additional resources. Practically, however, this very rarely happens and it is important to encourage staff at lower levels to participate.</p>
<p>The main advantage of this type of communication is that it helps to maintain the discipline of staff at lower levels. It also protects the seniority of staff at the middle levels.</p>
<p>The main disadvantage is that the middle level staff management may refuse to forward the grievances coming from the lower level staff. For example, a sister in charge of a ward may refuse to pass information from junior nurses to the matron in charge of the hospital.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-4f1c3822.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="horizontal-communication">Horizontal Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#horizontal-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In horizontal communication the communication flow occurs between heads of departments or supervisors who are at the same level. The nurses in-charge of medical and surgical departments/wards consult one another. The supervisors at the same level exchange ideas on common goals in order to improve the quality of patient care. The supervisors may discuss the common problems affecting their departments with a view of getting solutions to recommend to the top management for approval.</p>
<p>Horizontal communication also occurs at the health centre and dispensary levels when the staff consult one another. The main advantages of this type of communication are that it encourages free communication by all staff in the departments all the time and ensures that staff do not fear each other, thus improving interpersonal relationships.</p>
<p>You now know what formal communication is. Move on to informal communication.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="informal-communication">Informal Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#informal-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Informal communication is an unofficial form of communication between groups of people in the organisation. The messages are discussed casually and are not recognised by the management. Informal communication is also known as the 'grapevine'.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 387 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>The grapevine is a form of information containing some half-truths and may emanate from the staff at the lower or middle levels in the organisation. The grapevine is common in organisations where a certain cadre of staff feels that their needs are not being addressed or where top management fails to clarify issues or communicate effectively with the middle and lower level staff. The grapevine should not be ignored because it gives a warning of impending issues of concern to the employees. The top management should provide current information to minimise grapevine rumours. Grapevine communication also gives a chance to the colleagues to express their views.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="unconscious-communication">Unconscious Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#unconscious-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Unconscious communication is where a wrong meaning has been transferred because of the way the communication has been conveyed unconsciously to the receiver. Usually the sender of the message is unaware that their behaviour is sending the wrong signals. For example, if you appear quite casual when giving important information, the recipient will misinterpret the importance of the information because of the manner in which you speak. Therefore, it is important for health workers to be aware of unconscious communication.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-communication-process">The Communication Process<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-communication-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Consider the communication process, what takes place when you have a conversation or exchange letters with another person? What are the elements involved? What can go wrong? Make a note of your thoughts and then compare your answer with the following definition of the communication process.</p>
<p>The communication process can easily be defined as the passing of information from the sender to the receiver. The components of the communication process can be remembered using the acronym "MSCREFS" which stands for:</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>M</th><th>-</th><th>Message</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>S</td><td>-</td><td>Source</td></tr><tr><td>C</td><td>-</td><td>Channel</td></tr><tr><td>R</td><td>-</td><td>Receiver</td></tr><tr><td>E</td><td>-</td><td>Effects</td></tr><tr><td>F</td><td>-</td><td>Feedback</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>S - Social settings</p>
<p>The communication process is illustrated in the graphic below.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-f81bd210.jpeg" alt="img-2.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-2-barriers-to-effective-communication">Section 2: Barriers to Effective Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-2-barriers-to-effective-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Despite your best attempts to communicate with your patients or colleagues, you may fail because of certain barriers or factors that hinder effective communication. It is, therefore, important for you to know some of these barriers and how you can overcome them.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-barriers-to-communication-can-you-identify-from-this-graphic">What barriers to communication can you identify from this graphic?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-barriers-to-communication-can-you-identify-from-this-graphic" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Please think through all the possible barriers before starting this section.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain what is meant by a barrier to effective communication</li>
<li>Describe barriers that may affect the six elements of the communication process</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="barriers-to-communication">Barriers to Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#barriers-to-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Barriers are the factors that prevent effective communication. After being placed in a channel, the message may be interfered with by some disturbance which increases the difficulty in perception or prevents some elements of the message from reaching the receiver.</p>
<p>Barriers to effective communication may be due to any breakdown in the six elements of the communication process: source, message, channel, receiver, effects and social setting. In this section, you will look at all the six elements and see how each can contribute to a breakdown in communication.</p>
<p>The person who initiates the communication process is called the originating communicator or source of the message. You will now see how the source of the message can become a barrier to effective communication.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="barriers-resulting-from-the-source">Barriers Resulting from the Source<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#barriers-resulting-from-the-source" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The source of the message should have qualities that facilitate effective communication. Firstly, the source should have a sound understanding of their audience and a good knowledge of their subject. The audience determines the level of language and vocabulary to be used. When addressing illiterate peasants, one has to put oneself in their situation to be able to appreciate their culture, values, perceptions, worries and hopes. Failure to recognise the importance of these socio-cultural and psychological factors can lead to a breakdown in communication.</p>
<p>In addition to the semantic barriers, there are also physical barriers. These may be attributed to the climate, for example, very cold or very hot weather, wind, noise and so on.</p>
<p>System overload may occur where an individual sends or receives too much information at the same time. For example, a nurse may be taking over an evening shift and all of a sudden she is urgently called to attend to a telephone call from the matron. This will deflect her attention which will lead to communication breakdown.</p>
<p>The privacy and confidentiality of the patient when taking their history is important. Where privacy and confidentiality are not observed, the readiness of the patient to talk freely is severely restricted which can lead to a communication breakdown. The sender should use appropriate language according to the level and age of the receiver.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="barriers-affecting-the-message">Barriers Affecting the Message<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#barriers-affecting-the-message" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The other component of the communication process is the message. The message is what the sender wishes to convey to the audience. In order for the message to be well-received and effective, the sender must plan it well with the needs of the audience in mind. In other words:</p>
<ul>
<li>What does the sender want the receiver to know?</li>
<li>How do they expect the receiver to feel?</li>
<li>Do they want to change the behaviour of the receiver?</li>
</ul>
<p>Unless the sender plans their message with these factors in mind, the message is unlikely to have the desired effect on the audience.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="techniques-for-creating-effective-messages">Techniques for Creating Effective Messages<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#techniques-for-creating-effective-messages" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In order to avoid failure in communication, you must address the following factors:</p>
<ul>
<li>The message must be expressed in simple language. It must be short and to the point. The delivery of the message should involve proper communication, pauses and stressing of key words.</li>
<li>The message must be problem-centred. It must address a health concern or issue affecting the individual or the community.</li>
<li>The message should be culturally relevant and not offensive to the values and beliefs of the community or individuals. Religious beliefs are particularly important.</li>
<li>The message must fall within the socio-economic abilities of the audience. Do not propose solutions that are beyond the reach of your audience.</li>
<li>The message must demonstrate that it is much more important and beneficial to do what is proposed in the message than what the message opposes.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="barriers-resulting-from-the-receiver">Barriers Resulting from the Receiver<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#barriers-resulting-from-the-receiver" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The next component of the communication process that can bring about communication breakdown is inadequate knowledge or understanding of the socio-economic and cultural factors surrounding the audience. Understanding the audience is key to successful communication.</p>
<p>The receiver is a very important element in the communication process.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="factors-in-a-communication-breakdown-at-the-receiver">Factors in a Communication Breakdown at the Receiver<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#factors-in-a-communication-breakdown-at-the-receiver" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>If the receiver of the message is inadequately prepared physically,</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>socially and psychologically about the venue and time of giving a health message, they may arrive late.</p>
<ul>
<li>If the receiver does not know the benefits to gain from the message, they may have little interest to listen to the message.</li>
<li>If the receiver of the message does not understand the language because it is expressed in complicated jargon. The sender must speak in a language that is familiar to the audience.</li>
<li>If the sender stammers and speaks inaudibly there will be communication breakdown because of poor delivery of message.</li>
<li>If the message is received in a noisy environment, then the receiver will not hear it well.</li>
<li>If the message is transmitted to the receiver when they are emotionally disturbed, there will be a communication breakdown because of lack of concentration.</li>
<li>If the message transmitted is against the religious beliefs of the community, the communication process will be ineffective. For example, sharing health messages with Catholics on artificial methods of family planning, especially condom use when they believe in natural family planning methods. There will be a conflict of interests leading to communication breakdown.</li>
<li>There will be a likely communication breakdown if the sender of the message does not know the socio-economic status of the community. This is because the sender and receiver will not be able to relate and share the meaning of the message in the same way.</li>
<li>If the message contains too much information, the receiver may not be able to cope with the information. They will be overwhelmed and confused.</li>
<li>If the message takes a long time to reach the receiver, the audience will change their priorities.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="barriers-resulting-from-the-social-setting">Barriers Resulting from the Social Setting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#barriers-resulting-from-the-social-setting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You have seen that the social setting is the environment in which the message is transmitted. The social setting creates 'noise'</p>
<p>which interferes with the message. This 'noise' can be anything that interferes with the message signal, or distracts the source or recipient, it is not limited to actual noises, it can be visual, olfactory, tactile, electronic, cultural, racial or age related.</p>
<p> The selected venue for receiving the message has different posters, which are not relevant to the health message given. The posters act as detractors thus decreasing the level of concentration.</p>
<p> The sender does not consider the social status of the audience. For example, when you are organising a health meeting, include respected persons in the society like chiefs, councillors and members of parliament. These are individuals that the community has accepted as their leaders.</p>
<p> The sender of the message must consider the age and marital status of the audience when planning the venue. This is because married people may not feel free to discuss certain issues in the presence of single people. Intergenerational communication is not easy so, in planning the message, the age differences must be borne in mind.</p>
<p> The sender does not consider cultural beliefs of the audience. For example, if you are giving a health message to some communities, where men and women do not mix easily, make an effort to address each group separately.</p>
<p> The message is not action-oriented. The message must tell individuals and community members what they should do in order to improve their health status</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="barriers-affecting-the-communication-channel">Barriers Affecting the Communication Channel<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#barriers-affecting-the-communication-channel" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Communication channels are the means by which a message travels from the source to the receiver.</p>
<ul>
<li>In verbal communication the sender may speak in such a low voice that the receiver cannot hear well. A good example is when one talks to a large crowd in a low voice without an amplifier. The crowd may not be able to follow the message.</li>
<li>When the channel selected to transmit the message is through the mass media like the radio, television, or the print media such as newspapers, films, and magazines without considering the socio-economic status of the receiver. Many in the audience may not have the means to access the media used.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 390 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>If you select a verbal communication channel without considering the age of the receiver, the message content, language and delivery might lead to breakdown with youth or older persons if their special needs are not addressed.</li>
</ul>
<p>Effective communication is often facilitated by using more than one channel. In other words, you might need to use two or more channels to achieve effective communication. For example a nurse might use a poster to show the various family planning methods and their spoken voice to explain how each method works, and for whom it is best suited. The nurse may even have a video of satisfied family planning users talking about their experiences. You can see that, used in this way, more than one channel can ensure that the message is successfully delivered.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="barriers-affecting-the-impact-effects-of-communication">Barriers Affecting the Impact/Effects of Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#barriers-affecting-the-impact-effects-of-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Effects are the outcomes resulting from the communication of a message. These outcomes could be new knowledge, change in attitudes, or change in behaviour. Getting the desired effects depends upon the successful communication of the message. A communication breakdown can occur as a result of problems in managing any or all of the components of the communication process. This is particularly important for a nurse in practice because a breakdown in communication can lead to serious consequences including loss of life.</p>
<ul>
<li>If the sender of the message fails to use the appropriate language and to prepare the audience on the importance of the message for the improvement of their health status.</li>
<li>The receiver of the message may be emotionally disturbed and, therefore, does not understand the message as intended. Failure to acquire knowledge will not influence the audience to change their attitudes and behaviours.</li>
<li>The sender of the message may fail to involve the receiver (audience) in the planning phase and, therefore, disregards the cultural beliefs of the community. For example, a male midwife sharing a health message with a group of women who believe only female midwives should conduct deliveries according to their customs. The message may not produce the intended effects because the wrong communication channel was used leading to a breakdown in communication.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="barriers-affecting-feedback">Barriers Affecting Feedback<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#barriers-affecting-feedback" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Feedback is another component of the communication process which can cause a breakdown in communication. Feedback is used to determine if the intended message is understood by the receiver (or audience). A breakdown in communication occurs when the sender receives a negative response indicating that the message is not understood.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="section-3-essential-organisational-communication">SECTION 3: ESSENTIAL ORGANISATIONAL COMMUNICATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-3-essential-organisational-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>In section two you explored the barriers to effective communication and how they interfere with effective communication. In this section you will learn some aspects of essential organisational communication.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Describe four forms of communication in detail</li>
<li>Explain how to present and disseminate reports</li>
<li>Explain how to write an official/business letter</li>
<li>Explain how to conduct meetings and take minutes effectively</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="the-importance-of-effective-communication">The Importance of Effective Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-importance-of-effective-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>The importance of effective communication in a health facility cannot be overstated. Doctors and nurses collaborate with each other to ensure the patients get the care they deserve. No single medical personnel can provide effective quality care without involving the others.</p>
<p>Nurses communicate with other medical personnel such as physiotherapists, laboratory technologists, pharmacists, nutritionists and so on every day during the course of their work. All cadres of medical personnel play different roles but share the same goal of providing quality care to their patients. In your practice you will have consulted with your colleagues before making important decisions concerning the care of your patients.</p>
<p>Effective communication in a health facility is important because it highlights the role each</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>professional is playing towards the care of the patients. It is through communication that the managers are able to harmonise the care of the patients.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="forms-of-communication">Forms of Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#forms-of-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Communication in a health facility may occur in four forms, namely:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="intrapersonal-communication">Intrapersonal Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intrapersonal-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Intrapersonal communication occurs when you communicate to yourself without verbalising. It is an imaginary conversation reflecting the individual's thoughts and feelings. Intrapersonal communication helps you to think critically about important issues before solving a problem. For example, when planning patient care, you think about the problems and the correct action to alleviate the problem. Intrapersonal communication is important before planning a health message to share with a group of people/patients. It is, therefore, an important part of planning the message. Its importance, however, lies in how successfully it is translated into action.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="interpersonal-communication">Interpersonal Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#interpersonal-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Interpersonal communication is face-to-face communication between two or more persons. This kind of communication may occur between nurses and their patients or other medical professionals. Interpersonal communication is very effective and you should be able to share health messages with the community/patients in order to change their attitudes and behaviours. For example, you can use this type of communication to persuade the patients to abandon a harmful cultural practice such as Female Genital Mutilation (FGM).</p>
<p>The advantage of interpersonal communication is that the audience can ask questions on unclear issues for clarification. They can also give their own views on the matter under discussion.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="components-in-interpersonal-communication">Components in Interpersonal Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#components-in-interpersonal-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>There are three primary sources of the message in any interpersonal communication. One study in communication determined the percentage that each component contributed to the message being conveyed.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Component</th><th>Contribution to overall message</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Spoken word</td><td>7%</td></tr><tr><td>---</td><td>---</td></tr><tr><td>Body posture and gestures</td><td>38%</td></tr><tr><td>Voice tone and inflection</td><td>55%</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>From this breakdown you can see just how important it is to be aware of your body language and the tone of your voice when communicating. Only 7% of the message is conveyed by the words you are using, 93% is conveyed by things most people are not conscious of.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mass-communication">Mass Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mass-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Mass communication is a form of communication that is used to reach many people at the same time through the media of mass circulation or coverage, for example, television, radio and newspapers.</p>
<p>The mass media's contact with medical staff tends to coincide with major events such as vaccination campaigns, natural disasters or disease outbreaks. There have been times when health personnel have been recalled to duty using the mass media because of an emergency. Emergencies warranting communication through the mass media include times of war, disaster or disease outbreaks.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="organisational-communication">Organisational Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#organisational-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Organisational communication occurs between the management and the employees. This form of communication is necessary in order to achieve the desired goals of the organisation. It may occur between the managers, supervisors and all employees. The communication may occur vertically from the top management to all employees in the organisation or vertically when supervisors consult one another. Organisational communication also occurs between organisations with common interest.</p>
<p>Organisational communication is important because it explains the behaviours or conduct expected of the employees, for example, through circulars and documents. Organisational communication harmonises all activities performed by different technical and non-technical personnel in the institution. It also regularises the activities of the public and private institutions sharing common interests in the same locality for example public hospitals and non-governmental organisations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="written-communication">Written Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#written-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>You have now learnt the forms of communication which occur in a health facility. You shall now explore in detail two forms of written communications that are used in the health profession, namely, reports, and letters. First you will look at how to write a report in a health facility.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="presentation-of-reports">Presentation of Reports<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#presentation-of-reports" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Writing reports is nothing new to you, you have probably written several reports during your career to date. As a nurse in practice you may have presented a report to your colleagues or superiors. If you are working in a health centre or a dispensary you might have presented a report to the District Public Health Nurse or to the Medical Officer of Health (MOH) in charge of the district.</p>
<p>Nursing reports are written in the cardex and they cover a shift of 24 hours. Reports are presented to all nurses reporting in each shift. The number of shifts differ from hospital to hospital but three main shifts are the most common. The three shifts cover morning, afternoon and night duty. In each of these shifts, nurses write a report about the condition of the patients and any special investigation done. The report is important for continuation of care. The afternoon shift nurses write another report detailing the very sick patients in the ward and forward them to the matron on night duty. If you are working in a health centre/dispensary, you write a report on monthly basis for presentation to the District Public Health Nurse.</p>
<p>The aim of writing a report is to inform the authorities or other members of staff about what is happening in a unit or institution. A day shift report is given to inform the nurse taking over the shift of all the important activities or events which occurred in their absence. The report is required for effective continuity of patient care. A health centre or dispensary writes monthly and quarterly reports to inform the MOH and District Public Health Nurse of what has happened in the health facility over the last quarter or month. In this topic you will explore the principles of writing a report and you will see an example of how you should organise the content. You should also go through previous reports in the files in your health facility and then make a comparison to identify the differences.</p>
<p>When writing a report it is important for you to consider the following points:</p>
<ul>
<li>The purpose of writing the report</li>
<li>The type of information to be included in the report</li>
<li>The person(s) who will read the report</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-of-writing-a-good-report">Principles of Writing a Good Report<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-writing-a-good-report" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When writing a report, always keep in mind the following standards:</p>
<ul>
<li>Know the reason why you are writing a report</li>
<li>Know the subject matter you are writing about. The content should be factual</li>
<li>Omit your opinions from sections concerned with facts</li>
<li>Keep the report accurate, relevant and concise</li>
<li>Organise your points in a logical manner. All the related ideas should follow each other</li>
<li>The main ideas or key points in the report should be highlighted</li>
<li>When writing a report always start with the most pressing problem which needs immediate action</li>
<li>Use a language suitable to the reader. Write in a simple and clear language that the reader will understand</li>
<li>Use clear headings for each section of the report. A new paragraph should be started for unrelated ideas</li>
<li>Use your judgement and experience when suggesting actions or making recommendations to the reader/authority</li>
<li>The report should always emphasise ideas or facts which provide solutions to the problems</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="report-styles">Report Styles<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#report-styles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The hospital authorities or the Ministry of Health should give you guidelines on the format to be followed when writing a report. The style of writing the report should be logical and acceptable to the reader. The following information will help you to write a good report:</p>
<ul>
<li>Give information related to the main activities/events which have taken place since last year's report.</li>
<li>Indicate the problems you have experienced and how you dealt with them.</li>
<li>Give recommendations or suggestions on what the authority should do.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Indicate the decisions you want the authority/MOH to rectify and emphasise ideas which help the reader to come up with solutions to the problems.</li>
</ul>
<p>A Health Centre Report consists of four main sections.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="staff">Staff<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#staff" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Total number</li>
<li>New members</li>
<li>Resignations</li>
<li>Transfers</li>
<li>Retirees</li>
<li>Sick leave</li>
<li>Staff on leave</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cadres-of-staff">Cadres of Staff<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cadres-of-staff" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Clinical officers</li>
<li>Laboratory technicians</li>
<li>Public Health Technicians</li>
<li>Enrolled Community Health Nurses</li>
<li>Enrolled Nurse/Midwives</li>
<li>Statistical clerks</li>
<li>Subordinate staff</li>
<li>Driver(s)</li>
<li>Watchmen</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="cases-seen">Cases Seen<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cases-seen" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>New cases</li>
<li>Reattendances</li>
<li>Referred</li>
<li>Deaths</li>
<li>No of deliveries</li>
<li>Supply of drugs</li>
<li>Supply of vaccines</li>
<li>Reproductive health services and breakdown according to methods</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="problems-experienced">Problems Experienced<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#problems-experienced" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should report all the problems which according to your opinion are affecting the normal functioning of the health facility. You should also be able to identify the problems which need the attention and support of your superiors.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="examples-of-problems-experienced">Examples of Problems Experienced<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#examples-of-problems-experienced" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Staff failing to come on duty without good reason/permission</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Complaints presented by the staff</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Complaints presented by the community leaders/health service consumers</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mechanical breakdowns of vehicles and the estimated cost of repairs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Amount of money collected through cost-sharing during the period of reporting</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Drugs received (drug kit) and whether it was adequate to meet the needs of the patients</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Broken equipment needing repairs and the estimated cost</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The outbreak of a disease should first be reported through the phone immediately</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>When you are writing a report always remember to start with the most pressing problem indicating its urgency. The description of the problem should be accurate and very clear. You should emphasise the action which the authorities should take after reading the report.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="writing-a-negative-incidence-accident-report">Writing a Negative Incidence/Accident Report<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#writing-a-negative-incidence-accident-report" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>During your employment as a nurse perhaps you have witnessed several accidents happening in the ward. If you have ever witnessed an accident, consider the following questions:
 What was the nature of the accident?
 What action did you take when the accident occurred?
 What is the general policy of your health facility regarding patient accidents in the wards?</p>
<p>A Negative Incidence Report is a formal statement on any unusual event occurring in a nursing unit/ward with a risk of possible legal action. A legal action may be taken against the hospital by the patient or relatives for negligence or malpractice. The patient may claim a colossal amount of money in damages for injuries sustained, including developing bedsores. The purpose of a Negative Incidence Report is to inform the employer of the unusual incident which has occurred. The report is important as it will serve as evidence in case a law suit is launched by the patient.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="incidents-requiring-a-negative-incidence-accident-report">Incidents Requiring a Negative Incidence/Accident Report<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#incidents-requiring-a-negative-incidence-accident-report" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>A patient committing suicide in the ward</li>
<li>A child absconding from the ward</li>
<li>A patient falling from the bed and sustaining injuries</li>
<li>A patient sustaining burns in the ward</li>
<li>A patient being given wrong medication</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>A nurse fighting with a mentally ill patient</li>
<li>Wrong identification of a patient leading to wrong treatment or surgical intervention</li>
</ul>
<p>You can probably think of a number of incidents where a nurse had to write a negative report during your nursing practice. Most hospitals have policy guidelines on what action nurses should take when accidents occur. A nurse who is on duty when an accident occurs should write a statement to describe what happened.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-for-writing-a-negative-incident-statement">Principles for Writing a Negative Incident Statement<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-for-writing-a-negative-incident-statement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>The hospital accident reporting form should be completed in triplicate. One copy goes to the hospital authorities, the second copy is retained in the ward and the third copy is kept in the patient's file.</li>
<li>The statement should be concise, brief, clear, unambiguous and non-emotional.</li>
<li>It is a factual report. Write only the facts without exaggeration.</li>
<li>Write the events that occurred at the time of the accident.</li>
<li>Quantify the observable damage. For example, if it is a burn, indicate the extent in centimetres.</li>
<li>The writing should be legible, avoiding use of medical terms and abbreviations.</li>
<li>State only the truth of exactly what you saw with your own eyes.</li>
<li>Write down the names of all the witnesses who saw the accident happening including staff on duty.</li>
<li>Give an accurate date and time when the accident occurred.</li>
<li>Describe the immediate action which you took after the accident occurred, that is:</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>The first aid you offered to the patient</li>
<li>The observations you made</li>
<li>Informing the doctor to come to review the condition of the patient</li>
<li>The time the doctor came to see the patient</li>
<li>The immediate investigations ordered by the doctor and the findings</li>
<li>Medications prescribed after reviewing the patient</li>
</ul>
<ol start="11">
<li>The statement should include the name of the patient in full, diagnosis, inpatient number and the bed number.</li>
<li>When you have completed writing the statement, write your name in full, designation, and signature.</li>
</ol>
<p>You should write a Negative Incidence Report immediately after the incident before you forget the events that took place. Write a statement which does not incriminate you in a court of law.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="writing-appraisal-reports">Writing Appraisal Reports<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#writing-appraisal-reports" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The staff appraisal reports are written by the immediate supervisors in a ward or unit. Appraisal reports are written annually for each employee. The report gives a summary of an employee's performance and abilities for that period based on their job description.</p>
<p>The supervisor writing an appraisal report should be very objective and accurate. The information written on the report should reflect the actual behaviour of the employees without any bias. The report should be written in a balanced manner, giving the strengths and weaknesses of the appraised.</p>
<p>Depending on the format of the appraisal form, the employee being appraised may be required to complete the form too, following a certain criteria.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="contents-of-an-appraisal-report">Contents of an Appraisal Report<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#contents-of-an-appraisal-report" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In summary, an appraisal report should consist of the following information:</p>
<ul>
<li>Qualifications of the appraisee</li>
<li>Seniority/experience</li>
<li>Ability to perform assignments</li>
<li>Strengths</li>
<li>Character</li>
<li>Relationships with co-workers</li>
<li>Areas needing improvements</li>
<li>Recommendation for competency</li>
<li>Recommendation for training/promotion</li>
</ul>
<p>When you complete writing the appraisal report, discuss it with each employee. The appraisee should be allowed to read the report and make comments if necessary.</p>
<p>The other form of communication which is common in the health facility is the official letter.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="writing-an-official-letter">Writing an Official Letter<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#writing-an-official-letter" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Writing official letters is a rare activity for many employees in an organisation, letters are sometimes written when it is necessary to inform the employer about important occurrences. Letters are also written to request transfers to another station, to apply for study leave, or to request promotion. Whatever the reason for writing a letter, the structure of an official letter is the same. In this section you will learn the correct way of writing an official letter.</p>
<p>Bishops Computers
Bishops Computers</p>
<p>Our Reference / Your Reference: 'Our Reference' is always followed by a number. It links the letter to another communication in organisation and sometimes to a file number. It helps to trace the earlier communication/record maintained in the organisation. 'Your Reference' is usually the reference quoted in the letter to which you are replying. It also makes it easier to trace the communication in the filing cabinet.</p>
<p>Date: All letters should have a date. This makes it easier to file in a correct chronological order. The month should be written in full without abbreviations, for example, 4th December 2001.</p>
<p>Receiver's Name and Address: 'Mr' is the title commonly used for men. 'Ms' is used for women instead of 'Miss/Mrs' because it refers to both without indicating whether an individual is married or unmarried. 'Miss' or 'Mrs' should be used only if you know the marital status of the individual. The address should be written in full.</p>
<p>FAO: Short for 'For the Attention Of'. The attention indicator refers to the officer/person taking action on the letter.</p>
<p>Salutation: This is the opening greeting of a letter. It depends on how well you know the person you are addressing the letter to. However, in official letters, the usual form of salutation is indicated below:</p>
<ul>
<li>Dear Sir: This is used when you are writing a letter to an organisation or firm in general and not to an individual within it.</li>
<li>Dear Sir or Madam: Either of these is appropriate if you know the sex of the person you are writing to.</li>
<li>Dear Mr/Mrs/Miss/Ms: These are used to begin letters to people whom you have met or written before and are followed by the surname of the addressee, e.g. Dear Mr Johnson, Dear Mrs Petersen.</li>
</ul>
<p>Body of the letter: The body of a letter consists of:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A subject heading, the aim of which is to briefly and clearly state what the letter is about. For example, 'Your request for promotion' or 'Your notice of intention to retire'</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An introduction part or acknowledgement if there has been previous correspondence</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A second part which gives information and states the facts</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A final paragraph suggesting the action the reader of the letter should take</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Subscription or Complementary Close: This is the formal conclusion of the letter. Its form is decided by the form of salutation used, that is, letters beginning 'Dear Sir' or 'Dear Madam' should end with 'Yours faithfully'. Letters beginning 'Dear Mr/Mrs/Ms' should end with 'Yours sincerely'.</p>
<p>Letters beginning 'Dear Pilipili' can end less formally and on a warmer and more personal note, such as 'Yours', 'With best wishes' or 'Kind regards'. It should be done when the writer and the addressee know each other well.</p>
<p>Writer's Name and Signature: When a letter is typed, a space is left after the close of the letter for the writer to sign their name. The writer's name should appear in full, below the signature. Beneath this the position of the writer should be below the name. The employment identification number should be below the position.</p>
<p>Enclosures: Abbreviated as 'Enc.' is typed beneath the signature at the foot of the page. This is to remind the sender to enclose the item, and also make sure that the receiver notes this and does not discard it with the envelope.</p>
<p>PS: This stands for 'Post Scriptum'. This is used when adding something which has been left out from the body of the letter.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="layout-of-the-letter">Layout of the Letter<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#layout-of-the-letter" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The style described on the previous page is used when writing to any organisation or to a company. It is important to note the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>The sender's address appears at the right hand side of the page.</li>
<li>Each paragraph should be indented and begin about 1.5cm from the left hand margin. If paragraphs are not indented, then double spacing should be left between paragraphs.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishops Computers
Page 396 of 425
Bishops Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>The complementary close and the name typed beneath it should be at the centre at the foot of the page.</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260111-39488c7a.jpeg" alt="img-3.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="principles-of-letter-writing">Principles of Letter Writing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principles-of-letter-writing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are three basic principles you should keep in mind when writing any form of letter. These are courtesy, clarity and conciseness.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="courtesy">Courtesy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#courtesy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Courtesy is not only about using polite phrases such as 'your kind enquiry', but also showing consideration for your correspondent.
